Ingredients for 8 servings  CHICKEN  2 lb boneless, skinless chicken thighs (905 g) 1 tablespoon salt 1 teaspoon white pepper 1 cup cornstarch (125 g) 3 cups flour (375 g) 1 egg 1 Â½ cups water (360 mL) 2 tablespoons oil 6 cups oil (1 Â½ L), for frying ORANGE SAUCE  1 tablespoon oil Â¼ teaspoon chili flake 1 tablespoon garlic, minced Â½ teaspoon ginger, minced Â¼ cup sugar (50 g) Â¼ cup brown sugar (55 g) Â¼ cup orange juice (60 mL) Â¼ cup white distilled vinegar (60 mL) 2 tablespoons soy sauce 2 tablespoons water 2 tablespoons cornstarch 1 teaspoon sesame oil  Preparation On a cutting board, cut chicken into 1x1-inch (2x2-cm) cubes and set aside. In a medium mixing bowl, combine salt, white pepper, cornstarch, and flour. Whisk to combine. Add the egg, water, and oil until it reaches the consistency of pancake batter. Add the chicken to the batter and refrigerate at least 30 minutes. Heat oil in a wok or heavy bottom pan to 350ËšF (180ËšC). Gently add the chicken and cook for 5-6 minutes until lightly golden brown. Remove the chicken from the pan and transfer to a paper towel-lined plate. Set a heavy bottomed pot over medium- high heat and add the oil. Once the oil begins to shimmer, add the red pepper flakes, ginger, and garlic, and cook for 30 seconds, stirring constantly. Add the sugar and brown sugar, and stir to combine. Add in the orange juice and allow the sugars to begin to dissolve in the liquid, stirring occasionally. Add in the vinegar and soy sauce, and stir to combine. Add the cornstarch and water together and whisk to combine. Add to the pan and stir. Continue to cook the sauce until maple syrup consistency is achieved. Add in the fried chicken and stir until completely coated in the sauce. Top with sesame oil. Enjoy!

Modified recipe! (Thanks to yâ€™all in the comments. Basically I just halved the batter, used less of the flour and more water, removed the sesame oil, and doubled the sauce)  Chicken: 2 lb chicken (thighs) 1/2 tbsp salt 1/2 tsp white pepper 1/2 cup cornstarch 1 cup flour 1/2 egg 1 cup water 1 tbsp oil  Sauce: 2 tsp vegetable oil 1/2 tsp chili flakes 1 tsp ginger  2 tbsp garlic 1/2 cup white sugar 1/2 cup brown sugar  1/2 cup orange juice 1/2 cup vinegar 4 tbsp soy sauce 2 tbsp water+2 tbsp cornstarch mixed together (you may not need all of it, Iâ€™d say try and add it in slowly)  To make it: Cut the chicken into 1 inch cubes. Set aside. In a bowl, whisk the salt, white pepper, cornstarch, and flour together. Add the egg and the water. Whisk well to combine. Mix in the oil. Mix the chicken with the batter, and put it in the fridge for 30 minutes. Heat a pan with oil to 350F. Use tongs to gently place the chicken into the oil. Fry in batches, and make sure you fry the chicken for at least 6 minutes, or until golden brown.  Add oil, chilli flakes, ginger, garlic, both sugars in a pan. Turn the heat on (medium-low ish) and stir it. Add in the orange juice, let it boil a bit. Add the vinegar and soy sauce, and when itâ€™s boiling add in the water-cornstarch slurry slowly, while stirring. You may not need all of the slurry. Keep on stirring it until the sauce thickens, and add in the chicken. Stir, until the chicken is coated.  Serve while hot.

1.  If you're eating only for 1 or 2 people, that sauce will be enough.  If it's a family of 4 or more, double your sauce recipe. 2.  The batter should be equal parts flour and water.  2 cups should be sufficient. 3.  That cornstarch slurry will make your sauce very very thick.  Personally,I would do 1 TBSP cornstarch and 1 TBSP water.   4.  If you use a pot on the stove with oil, your chicken will take a long time to fry up. 5.  It probably wouldn't hurt to saute up some onions and peppers and maybe some mushrooms things like that to put over top of your finished dish. I think it would just add to it.

Honestly this recipe is one of the best ones out there but I did tweak a few things here and there which made it so much better!!  I used 700gms of boneless skinless chicken breast which is approximately 4 1/2 number of chicken breasts used :)  1. Firstly the batter, I actually made my own batter and it tasted so so so good so if you want an easier one just follow this: for 700gms of chicken I used 1 1/2 cup of flour with 1/2 cup of cornflour and a generous sprinkle of salt and black pepper, I then directly put my chicken into the dry mixture and coated it evenly. After that i added water accordingly. This ensures that the coating actually sticks to the chicken and since you add the water accordingly, you won't have excess batter that has to be dumped! then cover and chill for 30 mins before frying, like they said!  2. For the sauce, since  used 700gms of boneless and skinless chicken breast, I honestly just eyed the proportions for everything because i saw a comment which said that the quantity of sauce they make is only good for like 200gms of chicken. so I put like a tablespoon and a quarter of oil and a spoon full of chilliflakes. Added a small spoon full of garlic paste and a spoon full of ginger garlic paste! and then added 3 big spoons of white sugar and 1 and a half spoon of brown sugar, followed by 1/4 cup or orange juice and 1/4 cup of vinegar and 2 tablespoons of soy sauce. made a cornstarch slurry and added two spoons of it (just eye this part)  once it starts to thicken add the chicken and top it off with toasted sesame seeds. I skipped the sesame oil cause I didn't have it on hand but yes it tasted just as good without it.   This is so foolproof!! do let me know if you try this!! it worked for me and i hope it works for you:)

Total BS.  He is a liar.  Panda Express was not the originator of Orange Chicken in 1987.  We were serving orange chicken and orange beef back in the 1970's in my parents' restaurant.  And, we used real orange peels in our recipe, not orange juice. Also, we used white breast meat, not dark meat.  Orange Chicken and Orange Beef originated in the Hunan Province in China, not here in the US.

This recipe is amazing! Some suggestions for people just watching this and wanting to make:  1. With 2 lbs of chicken the dough quantity shown is way to much. In the dough keep everything the same except only use 1.5 cups of flour and 0.5 cups of starch. If dough is too hard add some more water until you get that pancake consistency.  2. If you don't have an oil thermometer, just fill the pan with oil and put the temperature high (but not all the way) and wait like 7 mins. Once you start cooking lower the temp to medium and you're golden.  3. DOUBLE EVERYTHING for the orange sauce. Just literally take all the numbers for the orange sauce and double them. It will make the perfect amount of sauce for 2 lbs of chicken. (could go a little easier on the vinegar also).  This will feed 5 very hungry people. Enjoy :)

TRIED OUT THE SAME EXACT RECIPE!! IT WAS REALLY GOOD!!   I would pay attention to the almost puree consistency when mince chopping the ginger and garlic.   I also added more water in the batter to achieve the same consistency as the one in the video.   Make sure you fry the chicken really well and be consistent with every batch. (I re-fried at a higher temp to still get that crunch after tossing it with the sauce)   Be patient with cooking out the cornstarch+water when you add it in order to achieve the almost syrup like consistency of the sauce or else if the sauce is too loose, it wont stick properly to the chicken and ur chicken wouldnt have that crisp on the outside. PLEASE READ THIS BEFORE YOU MAKE THIS!  I made this last week and it turned out fantastic however, there is a critical error in the directions. If you make this recipe with 3 cups of flour, 1 cup of corn starch and only add 1.5 cups of water, you will end up with a big ball of dough and nothing resembling pancake batter. I think they meant to say 2.5 cups of water. After adding the additional cup of water and enlisting a beater to help me get the lumps out, I was back in batter territory.  Keeping all that in mind, It will probably be a good idea to cut the batter recipe in half (adjust for the additional water if you do). With the recipe as they have described, you not only end up with way too much batter that will get dumped, you will spend extra time fishing through it trying to find all your chicken bits. Your tongs will get coated in batter and will probably make a bigger mess than necessary. Half way through the process, I ended up fishing all my chicken out and transferring them to a smaller bowl. Plenty of batter came with to the smaller and more manageable bowl and I ended up dumping the rest.   Finally, the sauce. Its not enough for the whole batch of chicken. Fortunately for me, my wife wanted some of the chicken without the sauce so I was saved. If you want enough sauce for the whole batch, you might want to make double the recipe, then, remove half the sauce from your frying pan and coat the chicken in batches. Probably two batches if you have a big frying pan. I don't think you can coat all the chicken at once (perhaps I'll try a wok next time).  Also on the sauce, mine thickened up fast once I added the corn starch...just.a little too think. Next time, I am going to be a little more deliberate in adding the starch to the sauce and might not add all of it.   Hope this helps! Family loved this and can't wait for me to make it again.

Listen up! I made this and it went well, I want to tell you my experience!  1. when making the batter, i'd say to only use 2 cups of flour (not 3), and add 2 cups of water (not 1.5)  2. if you wanna use black pepper instead of white, it went well for me. 3. when heating up the pot of oil, if you don't have a cooking thermometer, i'd say to put it at about medium-low heat. I initially made mine way too hot, and it does not need to be too hot at all. seriously. if you have numbers on your stove dial, i'd put it at "4" (if you want to check, at first, just put 1 nugget in the pot and leave it for 6 minutes, and see how it turns out. Then go from there.) 4. when making the sauce, keep in mind that you will not be putting all of the chicken in there. the sauce in the video will only be enough for about a quarter of the chicken you cooked.  5. I was only cooking for myself, and have been left with a bunch of leftover fried chicken. I am simply going to store it away for later, and just cook up some sauce whenever I want to have this dish again!

Panda Orange Chicken 2lbs Chicken Thigh (Hate dark meat so Breast for me please) Cut in small bite sizes add to mixing bowl Add 1tbsp of salt in ANOTHER BOWL with; 1 tsp white pepper  1 cup Cornstarch 3 cups flour 1 egg 1 Â½ Cup of Water     Whisk ingredients  Then add 2 tbsp of Oil Add chicken, cover and chill for 30 minutes Fry in batches (25pcs or at least 16pcs at a time) @ 350 degrees  SAUCE In a separate pan heat on med.  and mix; 1 tsp Vegetable Oil Â¼ tsp Chili Flakes Â½ tsp Ginger 1 tbsp Garlic Â¼ cup of Sugar Â¼ cup of Brown Sugar   Â¼ cup of Orange Juice (no pulp) Heat med High, bring to boil add; Â¼ cup of vinegar  2 tbsp Soy Sauce 2 tbsp Water + 2 tbsp cornstarch mix and slowly add to pan Stir until consistency is that of maple syrup Add chicken, mix thoroughly then add; 1 tsp Sesame Oil continue to stir until distributed throughout all the chicken. Serve!

Just finished making this. Here are some things I learned. 1. Make a half batch of batter for 2 pounds of chicken. This recipe makes wayyyyy too much batter.  2. You will need more water for the batter. If you do a half batch of batter use just over 1 and 1/4 cups of water. If you do a full batch use just over 2 and 1/2 cups. 3. This recipe does not make very much sauce. Double the measurements for the sauce when using 2 pounds of chicken. 4. Orange zest (grated orange peel) adds really good flavor and I would 100% recommend. About 1 teaspoon. 5. It is wise to cut the chicken a little smaller than 1in pieces. 6. Sesame oil is not necessary. 7. I prefer to use coconut oil instead of vegetable oil when making the sauce.  It tasted great! Better than the orange chicken at an actual Panda Express. :)

Orange chicken is a variation of General Tso's chicken â€” and was invented in the kitchens of Panda Express. Panda Express co-founder Andrew Cherng told NPR's The Salt that Chef Andy Kao created orange chicken one fateful day in Hawaii in 1987. Originally, it was served bone-in - but customers there didn't like the bones, so Kao developed a boneless version of the chicken and an American-Chinese staple was born. In China, General Tso is far better known for his battle prowess than for his chicken.
